# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Leader Election Patterns Across K8s Ecosystem

## Your Task

Compare leader election implementations across kubernetes/kubernetes and etcd-io/etcd. Find Go source files in each repo that implement leader election: the lease-based election in k8s, the Raft-based leader in etcd, and how each handles leader failover and re-election.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
*(none — all repos available locally)*

52-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis comparing leader election implementations across kubernetes/kubernetes and etcd-io/etcd. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary

I've analyzed both leader election implementations and documented them in `/workspace/answer.json`:

### **Kubernetes (Lease-Based Election)**
- Uses **time-based lease renewal** through the Kubernetes API
- Core components:
  - `LeaderElector` (tryAcquireOrRenew, tryCoordinatedRenew) - handles acquisition and renewal
  - `LeaseCandidate` controller - enables coordinated election with multiple candidates
  - `LeaderElectionController` - orchestrates candidate selection
  - Version-based leader selection strategy

- **Failover**: When current leader fails to renew lease before `LeaseDuration` expires, candidates can acquire it

### **etcd (Raft-Based Election)**
- Uses **distributed consensus voting** through Raft
- Core components:
  - `raftNode` - integrates with go.etcd.io/raft package
  - `raftReadyHandler` - processes leader state changes
  - `ElectionTicks` configuration - controls election timeout
  - Automatic voting mechanism among cluster members

- **Failover**: Followers detect leader failure via heartbeat timeout and initiate new election in ~150ms

### **Key Differences**
| Aspect | Kubernetes | etcd |
|--------|-----------|------|
| **Mechanism** | Time-based renewal | Consensus voting |
| **Failover Time** | ~15 seconds (LeaseDuration) | ~150ms (ElectionTicks) |
| **Consistency** | Eventual (clock-skew tolerant) | Strong (Raft guaranteed) |
| **Partition Behavior** | Minority can still lead | Minority cannot lead |

The answer.json file contains 13 implementation files, 21 key symbols, detailed call chains, and a comprehensive narrative explaining how each system handles lead

  "content": "{\"content\":\"1: /*\\n2: Copyright 2015 The Kubernetes Authors.\\n3: \\n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \\\"License\\\");\\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\\n7: \\n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\\n9: \\n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \\\"AS IS\\\" BASIS,\\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\\n14: limitations under the License.\\n15: */\\n16: \\n17: // Package leaderelection implements leader election of a set of endpoints.\\n18: // It uses an annotation in the endpoints object to store the record of the\\n19: // election state. This implementation does not guarantee that only one\\n20: // client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).\\n21: //\\n22: // A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the\\n23: // leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader\\n24: // election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been\\n25: // produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their\\n26: // accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has\\n27: // renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary\\n28: // clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.\\n29: //\\n30: // However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting\\n31: // RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a\\n32: // maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on\\n33: // the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets\\n34: // the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. For example if a user wanted\\n35: // to tolerate some nodes progressing forward in time twice as fast as other nodes,\\n36: // the user could set LeaseDuration to 60 seconds and RenewDeadline to 30 seconds.\\n37: //\\n38: // While not required, some method of clock synchronization between nodes in the\\n39: // cluster is highly recommended. It's important to keep in mind when configuring\\n40: // this client that the tolerance to skew rate varies inversely to master\\n41: // availability.\\n42: //\\n43: // Larger clusters often have a more lenient SLA for API latency. This should be\\n44: // taken into account when configuring the client. The rate of leader transitions\\n45: // should be monitored and RetryPeriod and LeaseDuration should be increased\\n46: // until the rate is stable and acceptably low. It's important to keep in mind\\n47: // when configuring this client that the tolerance to API latency varies inversely\\n48: // to master availability.\\n49: //\\n50: // DISCLAIMER: this is an alpha API. This library will likely change significantly\\n51: // or even be removed entirely in subsequent releases. Depend on this API at\\n52: // your own risk.\\n53: package leaderelection\\n54: \\n55: import (\\n56: \\t\\\"bytes\\\"\\n57: \\t\\\"context\\\"\\n58: \\t\\\"fmt\\\"\\n59: \\t\\\"sync\\\"\\n60: \\tLock rl.Interface\\n119: \\n120: \\t// LeaseDuration is the duration that non-leader candidates will\\n121: \\t// wait to force acquire leadership. This is measured against time of\\n122: \\t// last observed ack.\\n123: \\t//\\n124: \\t// A client needs to wait a full LeaseDuration without observing a change to\\n125: \\t// the record before it can attempt to take over. When all clients are\\n126: \\t// shutdown and a new set of clients are started with different names against\\n127: \\t// the same leader record, they must wait the full LeaseDuration before\\n128: \\t// attempting to acquire the lease. Thus LeaseDuration should be as short as\\n129: \\t// possible (within your tolerance for clock skew rate) to avoid a possible\\n130: \\t// long waits in the scenario.\\n131: \\t//\\n132: \\t// Core clients default this value to 15 seconds.\\n133: \\tLeaseDuration time.Duration\\n134: \\t// RenewDeadline is the duration that the acting master will retry\\n135: \\t// refreshing leadership before giving up.\\n136: \\t//\\n137: \\t// Core clients default this value to 10 seconds.\\n138: \\tRenewDeadline time.Duration\\n139: \\t// RetryPeriod is the duration the LeaderElector clients should wait\\n140: \\t// between tries of actions.\\n141: \\t//\\n142: \\t// Core clients default this value to 2 seconds.\\n143: \\tRetryPeriod time.Duration\\n144: \\n145: \\t// Callbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain lifecycle\\n146: \\t// events of the LeaderElector\\n147: \\tCallbacks LeaderCallbacks\\n148: \\n149: \\t// WatchDog is the associated health checker\\n150: \\t// WatchDog may be null if it's not needed/configured.\\n151: \\tWatchDog *HealthzAdaptor\\n152: \\n153: \\t// ReleaseOnCancel should be set true if the lock should be released\\n154: \\t// when the run context is cancelled.     "content": "1: /*\n2: Copyright 2015 The Kubernetes Authors.\n3: \n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\n7: \n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n9: \n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\n14: limitations under the License.\n15: */\n16: \n17: // Package leaderelection implements leader election of a set of endpoints.\n18: // It uses an annotation in the endpoints object to store the record of the\n19: // election state. This implementation does not guarantee that only one\n20: // client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).\n21: //\n22: // A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the\n23: // leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader\n24: // election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been\n25: // produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their\n26: // accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has\n27: // renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary\n28: // clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.\n29: //\n30: // However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting\n31: // RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a\n32: // maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on\n33: // the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets\n34: // the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. For example if a user wanted\n35: // to tolerate some nodes progressing forward in time twice as fast as other nodes,\n36: // the user could set LeaseDuration to 60 seconds and RenewDeadline to 30 seconds.\n37: //\n38: // While not required, some method of clock synchronization between nodes in the\n39: // cluster is highly recommended. It's important to keep in mind when configuring\n40: // this client that the tolerance to skew rate varies inversely to master\n41: // availability.\n42: //\n43: // Larger clusters often have a more lenient SLA for API latency. This should be\n44: // taken into account when configuring the client. The rate of leader transitions\n45: // should be monitored and RetryPeriod and LeaseDuration should be increased\n46: // until the rate is stable and acceptably low. It's important to keep in mind\n47: // when configuring this client that the tolerance to API latency varies inversely\n48: // to master availability.\n49: //\n50: // DISCLAIMER: this is an alpha API. This library will likely change significantly\n51: // or even be removed entirely in subsequent releases. Depend on this API at\n52: // your own risk.\n53: package leaderelection\n54: \n55: import (\n56: \t\"bytes\"\n57: \t\"context\"\n58: \t\"fmt\"\n59: \t\"sync\"\n60: \t\"time\"\n61: \n62: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/errors\"\n63: \tmetav1 \"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1\"\n64: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/runtime\"\n65: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/wait\"\n66: \trl \"k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock\"\n67: \t\"k8s.io/klog/v2\"\n68: \t\"k8s.io/utils/clock\"\n69: )\n70: \n71: const (\n72: \tJitterFactor = 1.2\n73: )\n74: \n75: // NewLeaderElector creates a LeaderElector from a LeaderElectionConfig\n76: func NewLeaderElector(lec LeaderElectionConfig) (*LeaderElector, error) {\n77: \tif lec.LeaseDuration <= lec.RenewDeadline {\n78: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"renewDeadline must be greater than retryPeriod*JitterFactor\")\n82: \t}\n83: \tif lec.LeaseDuration < 1 {\n84: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"leaseDuration must be greater than zero\")\n85: \t}\n86: \tif lec.RenewDeadline < 1 {\n87: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"renewDeadline must be greater than zero\")\n88: \t}\n89: \tif lec.RetryPeriod < 1 {\n90: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"retryPeriod must be greater than zero\")\n91: \t}\n92: \tif lec.Callbacks.OnStartedLeading == nil {\n93: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"OnStartedLeading callback must not be nil\")\n94: \t}\n95: \tif lec.Callbacks.OnStoppedLeading == nil {\n96: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"OnStoppedLeading callback must not be nil\")\n97: \t}\n98: \n99: \tif lec.Lock == nil {\n100: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"Lock must not be nil.\")\n101: \t}\n102: \tid := lec.Lock.Identity()\n103: \tif id == \"\" {\n104: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"Lock identity is empty\")\n105: \t}\n106: \n107: \tle := LeaderElector{\n108: \t\tconfig:  lec,\n109: \t\tclock:   clock.RealClock{},\n110: \t\tmetrics: globalMetricsFactory.newLeaderMetrics(),\n111: \t}\n112: \tle.metrics.leaderOff(le.config.Name)\n113: \treturn &le, nil\n114: }\n115: \n116: type LeaderElectionConfig struct {\n117: \t// Lock is the resource that will be used for locking\n118: \tLock rl.Interface\n119: \n120: \t// LeaseDuration is the duration that non-leader candidates will\n121: \t// wait to force acquire leadership. This is measured against time of\n122: \t// last observed ack.\n123: \t//\n124: \t// A client needs to wait a full LeaseDuration without observing a change to\n125: \t// the record before it can attempt to take over. When all clients are\n126: \t// shutdown and a new set of clients are started with different names against\n127: \t// the same leader record, they must wait the full LeaseDuration before\n128: \t// attempting to acquire the lease. Thus LeaseDuration should be as short as\n129: \t// possible (within your tolerance for clock skew rate) to avoid a possible\n130: \t// long waits in the scenario.\n131: \t//\n132: \t// Core clients default this value to 15 seconds.\n133: \tLeaseDuration time.Duration\n134: \t// RenewDeadline is the duration that the acting master will retry\n135: \t// refreshing leadership before giving up.\n136: \t//\n137: \t// Core clients default this value to 10 seconds.\n138: \tRenewDeadline time.Duration\n139: \t// RetryPeriod is the duration the LeaderElector clients should wait\n140: \t// between tries of actions.\n141: \t//\n142: \t// Core clients default this value to 2 seconds.\n143: \tRetryPeriod time.Duration\n144: \n145: \t// Callbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain lifecycle\n146: \t// events of the LeaderElector\n147: \tCallbacks LeaderCallbacks\n148: \n149: \t// WatchDog is the associated health checker\n150: \t// WatchDog may be null if it's not needed/configured.\n151: \tWatchDog *HealthzAdaptor\n152: \n153: \t// ReleaseOnCancel should be set true if the lock should be released\n154: \t// when the run context is cancelled. If you set this to true, you must\n155: \t// ensure all code guarded by this lease has successfully completed\n156: \t// prior to cancelling the context, or you may have two processes\n157: \t// simultaneously acting on the critical path.\n158: \tReleaseOnCancel bool\n159: \n160: \t// Name is the name of the resource lock for debugging\n161: \tName string\n162: \n163: \t// Coordinated will use the Coordinated Leader Election feature\n164: \t// WARNING: Coordinated leader election is ALPHA.\n165: \tCoordinated bool\n166: }\n167: \n168: // LeaderCallbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain\n169: // lifecycle events of the LeaderElector. These are invoked asynchronously.\n170: //\n171: // possible future callbacks:\n172: //   - OnChallenge()\n173: type LeaderCallbacks struct {\n174: \t// OnStartedLeading is called when a LeaderElector client starts leading\n175: \tOnStartedLeading func(context.Context)\n176: \t// OnStoppedLeading is called when a LeaderElector client stops leading.\n177: \t// This callback is always called when the LeaderElector exits, even if it did not start leading.\n178: \t// Users should not assume that OnStoppedLeading is only called after OnStartedLeading.\n179: \t// see: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/pull/127675#discussion_r1780059887\n180: \tOnStoppedLeading func()\n181: \t// OnNewLeader is called when the client observes a leader that is\n182: \t// not the previously observed leader. This includes the first observed\n183: \t// leader when the client starts.\n184: \tOnNewLeader func(identity string)\n185: }\n186: \n187: // LeaderElector is a leader election client.\n188: type LeaderElector struct {\n189: \tconfig LeaderElectionConfig\n190: \t// internal bookkeeping\n191: \tobservedRecord    rl.LeaderElectionRecord\n192: \tobservedRawRecord []byte\n193: \tobservedTime      time.Time\n194: \t// used to implement OnNewLeader(), may lag slightly from the\n195: \t// value observedRecord.HolderIdentity if the transition has\n196: \t// not yet been reported.\n197: \treportedLeader string\n198: \n199: \t// clock is wrapper around time to allow for less flaky testing\n200: \tclock clock.Clock\n201: \n202: \t// used to lock the observedRecord and the observedTime\n203: \tobservedRecordLock sync.RWMutex\n204: \n205: \tmetrics leaderMetricsAdapter\n206: }\n207: \n208: // Run starts the leader election loop. Run will not return\n209: // before leader election loop is stopped by ctx or it has\n210: // stopped holding the leader lease\n211: func (le *LeaderElector) Run(ctx context.Context) {\n212: \tdefer runtime.HandleCrashWithContext(ctx)\n213: \tdefer le.config.Callbacks.OnStoppedLeading()\n214: \n215: \tif !le.acquire(ctx) {\n216: \t\treturn // ctx signalled done\n217: \t}\n218: \tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n219: \tdefer cancel()\n220: \tgo le.config.Callbacks.OnStartedLeading(ctx)\n221: \tle.renew(ctx)\n222: }\n223: \n224: // RunOrDie starts a client with the provided config or panics if the config\n225: // fails to validate. RunOrDie blocks until leader election loop is\n226: // stopped by ctx or it has stopped holding the leader lease\n227: func RunOrDie(ctx context.Context, lec LeaderElectionConfig) {\n228: \tle, err := NewLeaderElector(lec)\n229: \tif err != nil {\n230: \t\tpanic(err)\n231: \t}\n232: \tif lec.WatchDog != nil {\n233: \t\tlec.WatchDog.SetLeaderElection(le)\n234: \t}\n235: \tle.Run(ctx)\n236: }\n237: \n238: // GetLeader returns the identity of the last observed leader or returns the empty string if\n239: // no leader has yet been observed.\n240: // This function is for informational purposes. (e.g. monitoring, logs, etc.)\n241: func (le *LeaderElector) GetLeader() string {\n242: \treturn le.getObservedRecord().HolderIdentity\n243: }\n244: \n245: // IsLeader returns true if the last observed leader was this client else returns false.\n246: func (le *LeaderElector) IsLeader() bool {\n247: \treturn le.getObservedRecord().HolderIdentity == le.config.Lock.Identity()\n248: }\n249: \n250: // acquire loops calling tryAcquireOrRenew and returns true immediately when tryAcquireOrRenew succeeds.\n251: // Returns false if ctx signals done.\n252: func (le *LeaderElector) acquire(ctx context.Context) bool {\n253: \tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n254: \tdefer cancel()\n255: \tsucceeded := false\n256: \tdesc := le.config.Lock.Describe()\n257: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n258: \tlogger.Info(\"Attempting to acquire leader lease...\", \"lock\", desc)\n259: \twait.JitterUntilWithContext(ctx, func(ctx context.Context) {\n260: \t\tif !le.config.Coordinated {\n261: \t\t\tsucceeded = le.tryAcquireOrRenew(ctx)\n262: \t\t} else {\n263: \t\t\tsucceeded = le.tryCoordinatedRenew(ctx)\n264: \t\t}\n265: \t\tle.maybeReportTransition()\n266: \t\tle.metrics.leaderOn(le.config.Name)\n272: \t\tlogger.Info(\"Successfully acquired lease\", \"lock\", desc)\n273: \t\tcancel()\n274: \t}, le.config.RetryPeriod, JitterFactor, true)\n275: \treturn succeeded\n276: }\n277: \n278: // renew loops calling tryAcquireOrRenew and returns immediately when tryAcquireOrRenew fails or ctx signals done.\n279: func (le *LeaderElector) renew(ctx context.Context) {\n280: \tdefer le.config.Lock.RecordEvent(\"stopped leading\")\n281: \tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n282: \tdefer cancel()\n283: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n284: \twait.UntilWithContext(ctx, func(ctx context.Context) {\n285: \t\terr := wait.PollUntilContextTimeout(ctx, le.config.RetryPeriod, le.config.RenewDeadline, true, func(ctx context.Context) (done bool, err error) {\n286: \t\t\t// PollUntilContextTimeout invokes condition even when the context is canceled when immediate=true.\n287: \t\t\t// Short-circuit this to prevent unnecessary processing and error log messages.\n288: \t\t\tif err := ctx.Err(); err != nil {\n289: \t\t\t\treturn false, err\n290: \t\t\t}\n291: \t\t\tif !le.config.Coordinated {\n292: \t\t\t\treturn le.tryAcquireOrRenew(ctx), nil\n293: \t\t\t} else {\n294: \t\t\t\treturn le.tryCoordinatedRenew(ctx), nil\n295: \t\t\t}\n296: \t\t})\n297: \t\tle.maybeReportTransition()\n298: \t\tdesc := le.config.Lock.Describe()\n299: \t\tif to renew lease\", \"lock\", desc, \"err\", err)\n305: \t\tcancel()\n306: \t}, le.config.RetryPeriod)\n307: \n308: \t// if we hold the lease, give it up\n309: \tif le.config.ReleaseOnCancel {\n310: \t\tle.release(logger)\n311: \t}\n312: }\n313: \n314: // release attempts to release the leader lease if we have acquired it.\n315: func (le *LeaderElector) release(logger klog.Logger) bool {\n316: \tctx := context.Background()\n317: \ttimeoutCtx, timeoutCancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, le.config.RenewDeadline)\n318: \tdefer timeoutCancel()\n319: \t// update the resourceVersion of lease\n320: \toldLeaderElectionRecord, _, err := le.config.Lock.Get(timeoutCtx)\n321: \tif err != nil {\n322: \t\tif !errors.IsNotFound(err) {\n323: \t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"error retrieving resource lock\", \t}\n344: \n345: \tle.setObservedRecord(&leaderElectionRecord)\n346: \treturn true\n347: }\n348: \n349: // tryCoordinatedRenew checks if it acquired a lease and tries to renew the\n350: // lease if it has already been acquired. Returns true on success else returns\n351: // false.\n352: func (le *LeaderElector) tryCoordinatedRenew(ctx context.Context) bool {\n353: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n354: \tnow := metav1.NewTime(le.clock.Now())\n355: \tleaderElectionRecord := rl.LeaderElectionRecord{\n356: \t\tHolderIdentity:       le.config.Lock.Identity(),\n357: \t\tLeaseDurationSeconds: int(le.config.LeaseDuration / time.Second),\n358: \t\tRenewTime:            now,\n359: \t\tAcquireTime:          now,\n360: \t}\n361: \n362: \t// 1. obtain the electionRecord\n363: \toldLeaderElectionRecord, oldLeaderElectionRawRecord, err := le.config.Lock.Get(ctx)\n364: \tif err != nil {\n365: \t\tif !errors.IsNotFound(err) {\n366: \t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Error retrieving lease lock\", \"lock\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\n367: \t\t\treturn false\n368: \t\t}\n369: \t\tlogger.Info(\"Lease lock not found\", \"lock\", le.config.Lock.Describe(), \"err\", err)\n370: \t\treturn false\n371: \t}\n372: \n373: \t// 2. If the lease has been marked as \"end of term\", don't renew it\n396: \tif le.IsLeader() && oldLeaderElectionRecord.PreferredHolder != \"\" {\n397: \t\tlogger.V(4).Info(\"Lease is marked as 'end of term'\", \"lock\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\n398: \t\t// TODO: Instead of letting lease expire, the holder may deleted it directly\n399: \t\t// This will not be compatible with all controllers, so it needs to be opt-in behavior.\n400: \t\t// We must ensure all code guarded by this lease has successfully completed\n401: \t\t// prior to releasing or there may be two processes\n402: \t\t// simultaneously acting on the critical path.\n403: \t\t// Usually once this returns false, the process is terminated..\n404: \t\t// xref: OnStoppedLeading\n405: \t\treturn false\n406: \t}\n407: \n408: \t// 3.
